Romeo!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What devil art thou, that dost torment me thus?<br>This torture should be roar'd in dismal hell.<br>Hath Romeo slain himself? say thou but 'I,'<br>And that bare vowel 'I' shall poison more<br>Than the death-darting eye of cockatrice:<br>I am not I, if there be such an I;<br>Or those eyes shut, that make thee answer 'I.'<br>If he be slain, say 'I'; or if not, no:<br>Brief sounds determine of my weal or woe.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I saw the wound, I saw it with mine eyes,--<br>God save the mark!--here on his manly breast:<br>A piteous corse, a bloody piteous corse;<br>Pale, pale as ashes, all bedaub'd in blood,<br>All in gore-blood; I swounded at the sight.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O, break, my heart! poor bankrupt, break at once!<br>To prison, eyes, ne'er look on liberty!<br>Vile earth, to earth resign; end motion here;<br>And thou and Romeo press one heavy bier!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O Tybalt, Tybalt, the best friend I had!<br>O courteous Tybalt! honest gentleman!<br>That ever I should live to see thee dead!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What storm is this that blows so contrary?<br>Is Romeo slaughter'd, and is Tybalt dead?<br>My dear-loved cousin, and my dearer lord?<br>Then, dreadful trumpet, sound the general doom!<br>For who is living, if those two are gone?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Tybalt is gone, and Romeo banished;<br>Romeo that kill'd him, he is banished.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O God! did Romeo's hand shed Tybalt's blood?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">It did, it did; alas the day, it did!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O serpent heart, hid with a flowering face!<br>Did ever dragon keep so fair a cave?<br>Beautiful tyrant! fiend angelical!<br>Dove-feather'd raven! wolvish-ravening lamb!<br>Despised substance of divinest show!<br>Just opposite to what thou justly seem'st,<br>A damned saint, an honourable villain!<br>O nature, what hadst thou to do in hell,<br>When thou didst bower the spirit of a fiend<br>In moral paradise of such sweet flesh?<br>Was ever book containing such vile matter<br>So fairly bound? O that deceit should dwell<br>In such a gorgeous palace!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">There's no trust,<br>No faith, no honesty in men; all perjured,<br>All forsworn, all naught, all dissemblers.<br>Ah, where's my man? give me some aqua vitae:<br>These griefs, these woes, these sorrows make me old.<br>Shame come to Romeo!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Blister'd be thy tongue<br>For such a wish! he was not born to shame:<br>Upon his brow shame is ashamed to sit;<br>For 'tis a throne where honour may be crown'd<br>Sole monarch of the universal earth.<br>O, what a beast was I to chide at him!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Will you speak well of him that kill'd your cousin?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Shall I speak ill of him that is my husband?<br>Ah, poor my lord, what tongue shall smooth thy name,<br>When I, thy three-hours wife, have mangled it?<br>But, wherefore, villain, didst thou kill my cousin?<br>That villain cousin would have kill'd my husband:<br>Back, foolish tears, back to your native spring;<br>Your tributary drops belong to woe,<br>Which you, mistaking, offer up to joy.<br>My husband lives, that Tybalt would have slain;<br>And Tybalt's dead, that would have slain my husband:<br>All this is comfort; wherefore weep I then?<br>Some word there was, worser than Tybalt's death,<br>That murder'd me: I would forget it fain;<br>But, O, it presses to my memory,<br>Like damned guilty deeds to sinners' minds:<br>'Tybalt is dead, and Romeo--banished;'<br>That 'banished,' that one word 'banished,'<br>Hath slain ten thousand Tybalts. Tybalt's death<br>Was woe enough, if it had ended there:<br>Or, if sour woe delights in fellowship<br>And needly will be rank'd with other griefs,<br>Why follow'd not, when she said 'Tybalt's dead,'<br>Thy father, or thy mother, nay, or both,<br>Which modern lamentations might have moved?<br>But with a rear-ward following Tybalt's death,<br>'Romeo is banished,' to speak that word,<br>Is father, mother, Tybalt, Romeo, Juliet,<br>All slain, all dead. 'Romeo is banished!'<br>There is no end, no limit, measure, bound,<br>In that word's death; no words can that woe sound.<br>Where is my father, and my mother, nurse?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Weeping and wailing over Tybalt's corse:<br>Will you go to them? I will bring you thither.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Wash they his wounds with tears: mine shall be spent,<br>When theirs are dry, for Romeo's banishment.<br>Take up those cords: poor ropes, you are beguiled,<br>Both you and I; for Romeo is exiled:<br>He made you for a highway to my bed;<br>But I, a maid, die maiden-widowed.<br>Come, cords, come, nurse; I'll to my wedding-bed;<br>And death, not Romeo, take my maidenhead!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hie to your chamber: I'll find Romeo<br>To comfort you: I wot well where he is.<br>Hark ye, your Romeo will be here at night:<br>I'll to him; he is hid at Laurence' cell.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O, find him! give this ring to my true knight,<br>And bid him come to take his last farewell.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt</em></p></blockquote><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">SCENE III. Friar Laurence's cell.</h3><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter FRIAR LAURENCE</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Romeo, come forth; come forth, thou fearful man:<br>Affliction is enamour'd of thy parts,<br>And thou art wedded to calamity.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter ROMEO</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Father, what news? what is the prince's doom?<br>What sorrow craves acquaintance at my hand,<br>That I yet know not?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Too familiar<br>Is my dear son with such sour company:<br>I bring thee tidings of the prince's doom.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What less than dooms-day is the prince's doom?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">A gentler judgment vanish'd from his lips,<br>Not body's death, but body's banishment.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ha, banishment! be merciful, say 'death;'<br>For exile hath more terror in his look,<br>Much more than death: do not say 'banishment.'<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hence from Verona art thou banished:<br>Be patient, for the world is broad and wide.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">There is no world without Verona walls,<br>But purgatory, torture, hell itself.<br>Hence-banished is banish'd from the world,<br>And world's exile is death: then banished,<br>Is death mis-term'd: calling death banishment,<br>Thou cutt'st my head off with a golden axe,<br>And smilest upon the stroke that murders me.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O deadly sin! O rude unthankfulness!<br>Thy fault our law calls death; but the kind prince,<br>Taking thy part, hath rush'd aside the law,<br>And turn'd that black word death to banishment:<br>This is dear mercy, and thou seest it not.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">'Tis torture, and not mercy: heaven is here,<br>Where Juliet lives; and every cat and dog<br>And little mouse, every unworthy thing,<br>Live here in heaven and may look on her;<br>But Romeo may not: more validity,<br>More honourable state, more courtship lives<br>In carrion-flies than Romeo: they my seize<br>On the white wonder of dear Juliet's hand<br>And steal immortal blessing from her lips,<br>Who even in pure and vestal modesty,<br>Still blush, as thinking their own kisses sin;<br>But Romeo may not; he is banished:<br>Flies may do this, but I from this must fly:<br>They are free men, but I am banished.<br>And say'st thou yet that exile is not death?<br>Hadst thou no poison mix'd, no sharp-ground knife,<br>No sudden mean of death, though ne'er so mean,<br>But 'banished' to kill me?--'banished'?<br>O friar, the damned use that word in hell;<br>Howlings attend it: how hast thou the heart,<br>Being a divine, a ghostly confessor,<br>A sin-absolver, and my friend profess'd,<br>To mangle me with that word 'banished'?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Thou fond mad man, hear me but speak a word.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O, thou wilt speak again of banishment.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I'll give thee armour to keep off that word:<br>Adversity's sweet milk, philosophy,<br>To comfort thee, though thou art banished.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Yet 'banished'? Hang up philosophy!<br>Unless philosophy can make a Juliet,<br>Displant a town, reverse a prince's doom,<br>It helps not, it prevails not: talk no more.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O, then I see that madmen have no ears.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">How should they, when that wise men have no eyes?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Let me dispute with thee of thy estate.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Thou canst not speak of that thou dost not feel:<br>Wert thou as young as I, Juliet thy love,<br>An hour but married, Tybalt murdered,<br>Doting like me and like me banished,<br>Then mightst thou speak, then mightst thou tear thy hair,<br>And fall upon the ground, as I do now,<br>Taking the measure of an unmade grave.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Knocking within</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Arise; one knocks; good Romeo, hide thyself.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Not I; unless the breath of heartsick groans,<br>Mist-like, infold me from the search of eyes.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Knocking</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hark, how they knock! Who's there? Romeo, arise;<br>Thou wilt be taken. Stay awhile! Stand up;<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Knocking</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Run to my study. By and by! God's will,<br>What simpleness is this! I come, I come!<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Knocking</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Who knocks so hard? whence come you? what's your will?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">[Within] Let me come in, and you shall know<br>my errand;<br>I come from Lady Juliet.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Welcome, then.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter Nurse</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O holy friar, O, tell me, holy friar,<br>Where is my lady's lord, where's Romeo?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">There on the ground, with his own tears made drunk.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O, he is even in my mistress' case,<br>Just in her case! O woful sympathy!<br>Piteous predicament! Even so lies she,<br>Blubbering and weeping, weeping and blubbering.<br>Stand up, stand up; stand, and you be a man:<br>For Juliet's sake, for her sake, rise and stand;<br>Why should you fall into so deep an O?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Nurse!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ah sir! ah sir! Well, death's the end of all.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Spakest thou of Juliet? how is it with her?<br>Doth she not think me an old murderer,<br>Now I have stain'd the childhood of our joy<br>With blood removed but little from her own?<br>Where is she? and how doth she? and what says<br>My conceal'd lady to our cancell'd love?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O, she says nothing, sir, but weeps and weeps;<br>And now falls on her bed; and then starts up,<br>And Tybalt calls; and then on Romeo cries,<br>And then down falls again.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">As if that name,<br>Shot from the deadly level of a gun,<br>Did murder her; as that name's cursed hand<br>Murder'd her kinsman. O, tell me, friar, tell me,<br>In what vile part of this anatomy<br>Doth my name lodge? tell me, that I may sack<br>The hateful mansion.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Drawing his sword</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hold thy desperate hand:<br>Art thou a man? thy form cries out thou art:<br>Thy tears are womanish; thy wild acts denote<br>The unreasonable fury of a beast:<br>Unseemly woman in a seeming man!<br>Or ill-beseeming beast in seeming both!<br>Thou hast amazed me: by my holy order,<br>I thought thy disposition better temper'd.<br>Hast thou slain Tybalt? wilt thou slay thyself?<br>And stay thy lady too that lives in thee,<br>By doing damned hate upon thyself?<br>Why rail'st thou on thy birth, the heaven, and earth?<br>Since birth, and heaven, and earth, all three do meet<br>In thee at once; which thou at once wouldst lose.<br>Fie, fie, thou shamest thy shape, thy love, thy wit;<br>Which, like a usurer, abound'st in all,<br>And usest none in that true use indeed<br>Which should bedeck thy shape, thy love, thy wit:<br>Thy noble shape is but a form of wax,<br>Digressing from the valour of a man;<br>Thy dear love sworn but hollow perjury,<br>Killing that love which thou hast vow'd to cherish;<br>Thy wit, that ornament to shape and love,<br>Misshapen in the conduct of them both,<br>Like powder in a skitless soldier's flask,<br>Is set afire by thine own ignorance,<br>And thou dismember'd with thine own defence.<br>What, rouse thee, man! thy Juliet is alive,<br>For whose dear sake thou wast but lately dead;<br>There art thou happy: Tybalt would kill thee,<br>But thou slew'st Tybalt; there are thou happy too:<br>The law that threaten'd death becomes thy friend<br>And turns it to exile; there art thou happy:<br>A pack of blessings lights up upon thy back;<br>Happiness courts thee in her best array;<br>But, like a misbehaved and sullen wench,<br>Thou pout'st upon thy fortune and thy love:<br>Take heed, take heed, for such die miserable.<br>Go, get thee to thy love, as was decreed,<br>Ascend her chamber, hence and comfort her:<br>But look thou stay not till the watch be set,<br>For then thou canst not pass to Mantua;<br>Where thou shalt live, till we can find a time<br>To blaze your marriage, reconcile your friends,<br>Beg pardon of the prince, and call thee back<br>With twenty hundred thousand times more joy<br>Than thou went'st forth in lamentation.<br>Go before, nurse: commend me to thy lady;<br>And bid her hasten all the house to bed,<br>Which heavy sorrow makes them apt unto:<br>Romeo is coming.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O Lord, I could have stay'd here all the night<br>To hear good counsel: O, what learning is!<br>My lord, I'll tell my lady you will come.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Do so, and bid my sweet prepare to chide.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Here, sir, a ring she bid me give you, sir:<br>Hie you, make haste, for it grows very late.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">How well my comfort is revived by this!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Go hence; good night; and here stands all your state:<br>Either be gone before the watch be set,<br>Or by the break of day disguised from hence:<br>Sojourn in Mantua; I'll find out your man,<br>And he shall signify from time to time<br>Every good hap to you that chances here:<br>Give me thy hand; 'tis late: farewell; good night.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">But that a joy past joy calls out on me,<br>It were a grief, so brief to part with thee: Farewell.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt</em></p></blockquote><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">SCENE IV. A room in Capulet's house.</h3><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter CAPULET, LADY CAPULET, and PARIS</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Things have fall'n out, sir, so unluckily,<br>That we have had no time to move our daughter:<br>Look you, she loved her kinsman Tybalt dearly,<br>And so did I:--Well, we were born to die.<br>'Tis very late, she'll not come down to-night:<br>I promise you, but for your company,<br>I would have been a-bed an hour ago.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">These times of woe afford no time to woo.<br>Madam, good night: commend me to your daughter.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I will, and know her mind early to-morrow;<br>To-night she is mew'd up to her heaviness.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Sir Paris, I will make a desperate tender<br>Of my child's love: I think she will be ruled<br>In all respects by me; nay, more, I doubt it not.<br>Wife, go you to her ere you go to bed;<br>Acquaint her here of my son Paris' love;<br>And bid her, mark you me, on Wednesday next--<br>But, soft! what day is this?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Monday, my lord,<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Monday! ha, ha! Well, Wednesday is too soon,<br>O' Thursday let it be: o' Thursday, tell her,<br>She shall be married to this noble earl.<br>Will you be ready? do you like this haste?<br>We'll keep no great ado,--a friend or two;<br>For, hark you, Tybalt being slain so late,<br>It may be thought we held him carelessly,<br>Being our kinsman, if we revel much:<br>Therefore we'll have some half a dozen friends,<br>And there an end. But what say you to Thursday?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">My lord, I would that Thursday were to-morrow.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Well get you gone: o' Thursday be it, then.<br>Go you to Juliet ere you go to bed,<br>Prepare her, wife, against this wedding-day.<br>Farewell, my lord. Light to my chamber, ho!<br>Afore me! it is so very very late,<br>That we may call it early by and by.<br>Good night.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt</em></p></blockquote><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">SCENE V. Capulet's orchard.</h3><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter ROMEO and JULIET above, at the window</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Wilt thou be gone? it is not yet near day:<br>It was the nightingale, and not the lark,<br>That pierced the fearful hollow of thine ear;<br>Nightly she sings on yon pomegranate-tree:<br>Believe me, love, it was the nightingale.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">It was the lark, the herald of the morn,<br>No nightingale: look, love, what envious streaks<br>Do lace the severing clouds in yonder east:<br>Night's candles are burnt out, and jocund day<br>Stands tiptoe on the misty mountain tops.<br>I must be gone and live, or stay and die.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Yon light is not day-light, I know it, I:<br>It is some meteor that the sun exhales,<br>To be to thee this night a torch-bearer,<br>And light thee on thy way to Mantua:<br>Therefore stay yet; thou need'st not to be gone.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Let me be ta'en, let me be put to death;<br>I am content, so thou wilt have it so.<br>I'll say yon grey is not the morning's eye,<br>'Tis but the pale reflex of Cynthia's brow;<br>Nor that is not the lark, whose notes do beat<br>The vaulty heaven so high above our heads:<br>I have more care to stay than will to go:<br>Come, death, and welcome! Juliet wills it so.<br>How is't, my soul? let's talk; it is not day.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">It is, it is: hie hence, be gone, away!<br>It is the lark that sings so out of tune,<br>Straining harsh discords and unpleasing sharps.<br>Some say the lark makes sweet division;<br>This doth not so, for she divideth us:<br>Some say the lark and loathed toad change eyes,<br>O, now I would they had changed voices too!<br>Since arm from arm that voice doth us affray,<br>Hunting thee hence with hunt's-up to the day,<br>O, now be gone; more light and light it grows.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">More light and light; more dark and dark our woes!<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter Nurse, to the chamber</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Madam!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Nurse?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Your lady mother is coming to your chamber:<br>The day is broke; be wary, look about.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Then, window, let day in, and let life out.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Farewell, farewell! one kiss, and I'll descend.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>He goeth down</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Art thou gone so? love, lord, ay, husband, friend!<br>I must hear from thee every day in the hour,<br>For in a minute there are many days:<br>O, by this count I shall be much in years<br>Ere I again behold my Romeo!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Farewell!<br>I will omit no opportunity<br>That may convey my greetings, love, to thee.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O think'st thou we shall ever meet again?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I doubt it not; and all these woes shall serve<br>For sweet discourses in our time to come.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O God, I have an ill-divining soul!<br>Methinks I see thee, now thou art below,<br>As one dead in the bottom of a tomb:<br>Either my eyesight fails, or thou look'st pale.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>ROMEO</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">And trust me, love, in my eye so do you:<br>Dry sorrow drinks our blood. Adieu, adieu!<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O fortune, fortune! all men call thee fickle:<br>If thou art fickle, what dost thou with him.<br>That is renown'd for faith? Be fickle, fortune;<br>For then, I hope, thou wilt not keep him long,<br>But send him back.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">[Within] Ho, daughter! are you up?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Who is't that calls? is it my lady mother?<br>Is she not down so late, or up so early?<br>What unaccustom'd cause procures her hither?<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter LADY CAPULET</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Why, how now, Juliet!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Madam, I am not well.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Evermore weeping for your cousin's death?<br>What, wilt thou wash him from his grave with tears?<br>An if thou couldst, thou couldst not make him live;<br>Therefore, have done: some grief shows much of love;<br>But much of grief shows still some want of wit.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Yet let me weep for such a feeling loss.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">So shall you feel the loss, but not the friend<br>Which you weep for.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Feeling so the loss,<br>Cannot choose but ever weep the friend.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Well, girl, thou weep'st not so much for his death,<br>As that the villain lives which slaughter'd him.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What villain madam?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">That same villain, Romeo.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">[Aside] Villain and he be many miles asunder.--<br>God Pardon him! I do, with all my heart;<br>And yet no man like he doth grieve my heart.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">That is, because the traitor murderer lives.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ay, madam, from the reach of these my hands:<br>Would none but I might venge my cousin's death!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">We will have vengeance for it, fear thou not:<br>Then weep no more. I'll send to one in Mantua,<br>Where that same banish'd runagate doth live,<br>Shall give him such an unaccustom'd dram,<br>That he shall soon keep Tybalt company:<br>And then, I hope, thou wilt be satisfied.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Indeed, I never shall be satisfied<br>With Romeo, till I behold him--dead--<br>Is my poor heart for a kinsman vex'd.<br>Madam, if you could find out but a man<br>To bear a poison, I would temper it;<br>That Romeo should, upon receipt thereof,<br>Soon sleep in quiet. O, how my heart abhors<br>To hear him named, and cannot come to him.<br>To wreak the love I bore my cousin<br>Upon his body that slaughter'd him!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Find thou the means, and I'll find such a man.<br>But now I'll tell thee joyful tidings, girl.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">And joy comes well in such a needy time:<br>What are they, I beseech your ladyship?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Well, well, thou hast a careful father, child;<br>One who, to put thee from thy heaviness,<br>Hath sorted out a sudden day of joy,<br>That thou expect'st not nor I look'd not for.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Madam, in happy time, what day is that?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Marry, my child, early next Thursday morn,<br>The gallant, young and noble gentleman,<br>The County Paris, at Saint Peter's Church,<br>Shall happily make thee there a joyful bride.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Now, by Saint Peter's Church and Peter too,<br>He shall not make me there a joyful bride.<br>I wonder at this haste; that I must wed<br>Ere he, that should be husband, comes to woo.<br>I pray you, tell my lord and father, madam,<br>I will not marry yet; and, when I do, I swear,<br>It shall be Romeo, whom you know I hate,<br>Rather than Paris. These are news indeed!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Here comes your father; tell him so yourself,<br>And see how he will take it at your hands.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter CAPULET and Nurse</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">When the sun sets, the air doth drizzle dew;<br>But for the sunset of my brother's son<br>It rains downright.<br>How now! a conduit, girl? what, still in tears?<br>Evermore showering? In one little body<br>Thou counterfeit'st a bark, a sea, a wind;<br>For still thy eyes, which I may call the sea,<br>Do ebb and flow with tears; the bark thy body is,<br>Sailing in this salt flood; the winds, thy sighs;<br>Who, raging with thy tears, and they with them,<br>Without a sudden calm, will overset<br>Thy tempest-tossed body. How now, wife!<br>Have you deliver'd to her our decree?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ay, sir; but she will none, she gives you thanks.<br>I would the fool were married to her grave!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Soft! take me with you, take me with you, wife.<br>How! will she none? doth she not give us thanks?<br>Is she not proud? doth she not count her blest,<br>Unworthy as she is, that we have wrought<br>So worthy a gentleman to be her bridegroom?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Not proud, you have; but thankful, that you have:<br>Proud can I never be of what I hate;<br>But thankful even for hate, that is meant love.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">How now, how now, chop-logic! What is this?<br>'Proud,' and 'I thank you,' and 'I thank you not;'<br>And yet 'not proud,' mistress minion, you,<br>Thank me no thankings, nor, proud me no prouds,<br>But fettle your fine joints 'gainst Thursday next,<br>To go with Paris to Saint Peter's Church,<br>Or I will drag thee on a hurdle thither.<br>Out, you green-sickness carrion! out, you baggage!<br>You tallow-face!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Fie, fie! what, are you mad?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Good father, I beseech you on my knees,<br>Hear me with patience but to speak a word.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hang thee, young baggage! disobedient wretch!<br>I tell thee what: get thee to church o' Thursday,<br>Or never after look me in the face:<br>Speak not, reply not, do not answer me;<br>My fingers itch. Wife, we scarce thought us blest<br>That God had lent us but this only child;<br>But now I see this one is one too much,<br>And that we have a curse in having her:<br>Out on her, hilding!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">God in heaven bless her!<br>You are to blame, my lord, to rate her so.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">And why, my lady wisdom? hold your tongue,<br>Good prudence; smatter with your gossips, go.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I speak no treason.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O, God ye god-den.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">May not one speak?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Peace, you mumbling fool!<br>Utter your gravity o'er a gossip's bowl;<br>For here we need it not.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">You are too hot.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">God's bread! it makes me mad:<br>Day, night, hour, tide, time, work, play,<br>Alone, in company, still my care hath been<br>To have her match'd: and having now provided<br>A gentleman of noble parentage,<br>Of fair demesnes, youthful, and nobly train'd,<br>Stuff'd, as they say, with honourable parts,<br>Proportion'd as one's thought would wish a man;<br>And then to have a wretched puling fool,<br>A whining mammet, in her fortune's tender,<br>To answer 'I'll not wed; I cannot love,<br>I am too young; I pray you, pardon me.'<br>But, as you will not wed, I'll pardon you:<br>Graze where you will you shall not house with me:<br>Look to't, think on't, I do not use to jest.<br>Thursday is near; lay hand on heart, advise:<br>An you be mine, I'll give you to my friend;<br>And you be not, hang, beg, starve, die in<br>the streets,<br>For, by my soul, I'll ne'er acknowledge thee,<br>Nor what is mine shall never do thee good:<br>Trust to't, bethink you; I'll not be forsworn.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Is there no pity sitting in the clouds,<br>That sees into the bottom of my grief?<br>O, sweet my mother, cast me not away!<br>Delay this marriage for a month, a week;<br>Or, if you do not, make the bridal bed<br>In that dim monument where Tybalt lies.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Talk not to me, for I'll not speak a word:<br>Do as thou wilt, for I have done with thee.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O God!--O nurse, how shall this be prevented?<br>My husband is on earth, my faith in heaven;<br>How shall that faith return again to earth,<br>Unless that husband send it me from heaven<br>By leaving earth? comfort me, counsel me.<br>Alack, alack, that heaven should practise stratagems<br>Upon so soft a subject as myself!<br>What say'st thou? hast thou not a word of joy?<br>Some comfort, nurse.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Faith, here it is.<br>Romeo is banish'd; and all the world to nothing,<br>That he dares ne'er come back to challenge you;<br>Or, if he do, it needs must be by stealth.<br>Then, since the case so stands as now it doth,<br>I think it best you married with the county.<br>O, he's a lovely gentleman!<br>Romeo's a dishclout to him: an eagle, madam,<br>Hath not so green, so quick, so fair an eye<br>As Paris hath. Beshrew my very heart,<br>I think you are happy in this second match,<br>For it excels your first: or if it did not,<br>Your first is dead; or 'twere as good he were,<br>As living here and you no use of him.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Speakest thou from thy heart?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">And from my soul too;<br>Or else beshrew them both.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Amen!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Well, thou hast comforted me marvellous much.<br>Go in: and tell my lady I am gone,<br>Having displeased my father, to Laurence' cell,<br>To make confession and to be absolved.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Marry, I will; and this is wisely done.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ancient damnation! O most wicked fiend!<br>Is it more sin to wish me thus forsworn,<br>Or to dispraise my lord with that same tongue<br>Which she hath praised him with above compare<br>So many thousand times? Go, counsellor;<br>Thou and my bosom henceforth shall be twain.<br>I'll to the friar, to know his remedy:<br>If all else fail, myself have power to die.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">ACT IV</h3><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">SCENE I. Friar Laurence's cell.</h3><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter FRIAR LAURENCE and PARIS</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">On Thursday, sir? the time is very short.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">My father Capulet will have it so;<br>And I am nothing slow to slack his haste.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">You say you do not know the lady's mind:<br>Uneven is the course, I like it not.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Immoderately she weeps for Tybalt's death,<br>And therefore have I little talk'd of love;<br>For Venus smiles not in a house of tears.<br>Now, sir, her father counts it dangerous<br>That she doth give her sorrow so much sway,<br>And in his wisdom hastes our marriage,<br>To stop the inundation of her tears;<br>Which, too much minded by herself alone,<br>May be put from her by society:<br>Now do you know the reason of this haste.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">[Aside] I would I knew not why it should be slow'd.<br>Look, sir, here comes the lady towards my cell.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter JULIET</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Happily met, my lady and my wife!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">That may be, sir, when I may be a wife.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">That may be must be, love, on Thursday next.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What must be shall be.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">That's a certain text.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Come you to make confession to this father?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">To answer that, I should confess to you.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Do not deny to him that you love me.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I will confess to you that I love him.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">So will ye, I am sure, that you love me.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">If I do so, it will be of more price,<br>Being spoke behind your back, than to your face.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Poor soul, thy face is much abused with tears.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">The tears have got small victory by that;<br>For it was bad enough before their spite.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Thou wrong'st it, more than tears, with that report.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">That is no slander, sir, which is a truth;<br>And what I spake, I spake it to my face.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Thy face is mine, and thou hast slander'd it.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">It may be so, for it is not mine own.<br>Are you at leisure, holy father, now;<br>Or shall I come to you at evening mass?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">My leisure serves me, pensive daughter, now.<br>My lord, we must entreat the time alone.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">God shield I should disturb devotion!<br>Juliet, on Thursday early will I rouse ye:<br>Till then, adieu; and keep this holy kiss.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O shut the door! and when thou hast done so,<br>Come weep with me; past hope, past cure, past help!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ah, Juliet, I already know thy grief;<br>It strains me past the compass of my wits:<br>I hear thou must, and nothing may prorogue it,<br>On Thursday next be married to this county.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Tell me not, friar, that thou hear'st of this,<br>Unless thou tell me how I may prevent it:<br>If, in thy wisdom, thou canst give no help,<br>Do thou but call my resolution wise,<br>And with this knife I'll help it presently.<br>God join'd my heart and Romeo's, thou our hands;<br>And ere this hand, by thee to Romeo seal'd,<br>Shall be the label to another deed,<br>Or my true heart with treacherous revolt<br>Turn to another, this shall slay them both:<br>Therefore, out of thy long-experienced time,<br>Give me some present counsel, or, behold,<br>'Twixt my extremes and me this bloody knife<br>Shall play the umpire, arbitrating that<br>Which the commission of thy years and art<br>Could to no issue of true honour bring.<br>Be not so long to speak; I long to die,<br>If what thou speak'st speak not of remedy.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hold, daughter: I do spy a kind of hope,<br>Which craves as desperate an execution.<br>As that is desperate which we would prevent.<br>If, rather than to marry County Paris,<br>Thou hast the strength of will to slay thyself,<br>Then is it likely thou wilt undertake<br>A thing like death to chide away this shame,<br>That copest with death himself to scape from it:<br>And, if thou darest, I'll give thee remedy.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O, bid me leap, rather than marry Paris,<br>From off the battlements of yonder tower;<br>Or walk in thievish ways; or bid me lurk<br>Where serpents are; chain me with roaring bears;<br>Or shut me nightly in a charnel-house,<br>O'er-cover'd quite with dead men's rattling bones,<br>With reeky shanks and yellow chapless skulls;<br>Or bid me go into a new-made grave<br>And hide me with a dead man in his shroud;<br>Things that, to hear them told, have made me tremble;<br>And I will do it without fear or doubt,<br>To live an unstain'd wife to my sweet love.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hold, then; go home, be merry, give consent<br>To marry Paris: Wednesday is to-morrow:<br>To-morrow night look that thou lie alone;<br>Let not thy nurse lie with thee in thy chamber:<br>Take thou this vial, being then in bed,<br>And this distilled liquor drink thou off;<br>When presently through all thy veins shall run<br>A cold and drowsy humour, for no pulse<br>Shall keep his native progress, but surcease:<br>No warmth, no breath, shall testify thou livest;<br>The roses in thy lips and cheeks shall fade<br>To paly ashes, thy eyes' windows fall,<br>Like death, when he shuts up the day of life;<br>Each part, deprived of supple government,<br>Shall, stiff and stark and cold, appear like death:<br>And in this borrow'd likeness of shrunk death<br>Thou shalt continue two and forty hours,<br>And then awake as from a pleasant sleep.<br>Now, when the bridegroom in the morning comes<br>To rouse thee from thy bed, there art thou dead:<br>Then, as the manner of our country is,<br>In thy best robes uncover'd on the bier<br>Thou shalt be borne to that same ancient vault<br>Where all the kindred of the Capulets lie.<br>In the mean time, against thou shalt awake,<br>Shall Romeo by my letters know our drift,<br>And hither shall he come: and he and I<br>Will watch thy waking, and that very night<br>Shall Romeo bear thee hence to Mantua.<br>And this shall free thee from this present shame;<br>If no inconstant toy, nor womanish fear,<br>Abate thy valour in the acting it.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Give me, give me! O, tell not me of fear!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hold; get you gone, be strong and prosperous<br>In this resolve: I'll send a friar with speed<br>To Mantua, with my letters to thy lord.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Love give me strength! and strength shall help afford.<br>Farewell, dear father!<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt</em></p></blockquote><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">SCENE II. Hall in Capulet's house.</h3><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter CAPULET, LADY CAPULET, Nurse, and two Servingmen</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">So many guests invite as here are writ.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit First Servant</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Sirrah, go hire me twenty cunning cooks.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Second Servant</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">You shall have none ill, sir; for I'll try if they<br>can lick their fingers.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">How canst thou try them so?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Second Servant</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Marry, sir, 'tis an ill cook that cannot lick his<br>own fingers: therefore he that cannot lick his<br>fingers goes not with me.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Go, be gone.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit Second Servant</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">We shall be much unfurnished for this time.<br>What, is my daughter gone to Friar Laurence?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ay, forsooth.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Well, he may chance to do some good on her:<br>A peevish self-will'd harlotry it is.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">See where she comes from shrift with merry look.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter JULIET</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">How now, my headstrong! where have you been gadding?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Where I have learn'd me to repent the sin<br>Of disobedient opposition<br>To you and your behests, and am enjoin'd<br>By holy Laurence to fall prostrate here,<br>And beg your pardon: pardon, I beseech you!<br>Henceforward I am ever ruled by you.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Send for the county; go tell him of this:<br>I'll have this knot knit up to-morrow morning.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I met the youthful lord at Laurence' cell;<br>And gave him what becomed love I might,<br>Not step o'er the bounds of modesty.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Why, I am glad on't; this is well: stand up:<br>This is as't should be. Let me see the county;<br>Ay, marry, go, I say, and fetch him hither.<br>Now, afore God! this reverend holy friar,<br>Our whole city is much bound to him.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Nurse, will you go with me into my closet,<br>To help me sort such needful ornaments<br>As you think fit to furnish me to-morrow?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">No, not till Thursday; there is time enough.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Go, nurse, go with her: we'll to church to-morrow.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt JULIET and Nurse</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">We shall be short in our provision:<br>'Tis now near night.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Tush, I will stir about,<br>And all things shall be well, I warrant thee, wife:<br>Go thou to Juliet, help to deck up her;<br>I'll not to bed to-night; let me alone;<br>I'll play the housewife for this once. What, ho!<br>They are all forth. Well, I will walk myself<br>To County Paris, to prepare him up<br>Against to-morrow: my heart is wondrous light,<br>Since this same wayward girl is so reclaim'd.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt</em></p></blockquote><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">SCENE III. Juliet's chamber.</h3><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter JULIET and Nurse</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ay, those attires are best: but, gentle nurse,<br>I pray thee, leave me to my self to-night,<br>For I have need of many orisons<br>To move the heavens to smile upon my state,<br>Which, well thou know'st, is cross, and full of sin.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter LADY CAPULET</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What, are you busy, ho? need you my help?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">No, madam; we have cull'd such necessaries<br>As are behoveful for our state to-morrow:<br>So please you, let me now be left alone,<br>And let the nurse this night sit up with you;<br>For, I am sure, you have your hands full all,<br>In this so sudden business.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Good night:<br>Get thee to bed, and rest; for thou hast need.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt LADY CAPULET and Nurse</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>JULIET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Farewell! God knows when we shall meet again.<br>I have a faint cold fear thrills through my veins,<br>That almost freezes up the heat of life:<br>I'll call them back again to comfort me:<br>Nurse! What should she do here?<br>My dismal scene I needs must act alone.<br>Come, vial.<br>What if this mixture do not work at all?<br>Shall I be married then to-morrow morning?<br>No, no: this shall forbid it: lie thou there.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Laying down her dagger</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What if it be a poison, which the friar<br>Subtly hath minister'd to have me dead,<br>Lest in this marriage he should be dishonour'd,<br>Because he married me before to Romeo?<br>I fear it is: and yet, methinks, it should not,<br>For he hath still been tried a holy man.<br>How if, when I am laid into the tomb,<br>I wake before the time that Romeo<br>Come to redeem me? there's a fearful point!<br>Shall I not, then, be stifled in the vault,<br>To whose foul mouth no healthsome air breathes in,<br>And there die strangled ere my Romeo comes?<br>Or, if I live, is it not very like,<br>The horrible conceit of death and night,<br>Together with the terror of the place,--<br>As in a vault, an ancient receptacle,<br>Where, for these many hundred years, the bones<br>Of all my buried ancestors are packed:<br>Where bloody Tybalt, yet but green in earth,<br>Lies festering in his shroud; where, as they say,<br>At some hours in the night spirits resort;--<br>Alack, alack, is it not like that I,<br>So early waking, what with loathsome smells,<br>And shrieks like mandrakes' torn out of the earth,<br>That living mortals, hearing them, run mad:--<br>O, if I wake, shall I not be distraught,<br>Environed with all these hideous fears?<br>And madly play with my forefather's joints?<br>And pluck the mangled Tybalt from his shroud?<br>And, in this rage, with some great kinsman's bone,<br>As with a club, dash out my desperate brains?<br>O, look! methinks I see my cousin's ghost<br>Seeking out Romeo, that did spit his body<br>Upon a rapier's point: stay, Tybalt, stay!<br>Romeo, I come! this do I drink to thee.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>She falls upon her bed, within the curtains</em></p></blockquote><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">SCENE IV. Hall in Capulet's house.</h3><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter LADY CAPULET and Nurse</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Hold, take these keys, and fetch more spices, nurse.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">They call for dates and quinces in the pastry.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter CAPULET</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Come, stir, stir, stir! the second cock hath crow'd,<br>The curfew-bell hath rung, 'tis three o'clock:<br>Look to the baked meats, good Angelica:<br>Spare not for the cost.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Go, you cot-quean, go,<br>Get you to bed; faith, You'll be sick to-morrow<br>For this night's watching.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">No, not a whit: what! I have watch'd ere now<br>All night for lesser cause, and ne'er been sick.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ay, you have been a mouse-hunt in your time;<br>But I will watch you from such watching now.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt LADY CAPULET and Nurse</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">A jealous hood, a jealous hood!<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter three or four Servingmen, with spits, logs, and baskets</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Now, fellow,<br>What's there?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>First Servant</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Things for the cook, sir; but I know not what.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Make haste, make haste.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit First Servant</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Sirrah, fetch drier logs:<br>Call Peter, he will show thee where they are.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Second Servant</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I have a head, sir, that will find out logs,<br>And never trouble Peter for the matter.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exit</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Mass, and well said; a merry whoreson, ha!<br>Thou shalt be logger-head. Good faith, 'tis day:<br>The county will be here with music straight,<br>For so he said he would: I hear him near.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Music within</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Nurse! Wife! What, ho! What, nurse, I say!<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Re-enter Nurse</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Go waken Juliet, go and trim her up;<br>I'll go and chat with Paris: hie, make haste,<br>Make haste; the bridegroom he is come already:<br>Make haste, I say.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Exeunt</em></p></blockquote><h3 style="white-space:pre-wrap;">SCENE V. Juliet's chamber.</h3><p class="" data-rte-preserve-empty="true" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter Nurse</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Mistress! what, mistress! Juliet! fast, I warrant her, she:<br>Why, lamb! why, lady! fie, you slug-a-bed!<br>Why, love, I say! madam! sweet-heart! why, bride!<br>What, not a word? you take your pennyworths now;<br>Sleep for a week; for the next night, I warrant,<br>The County Paris hath set up his rest,<br>That you shall rest but little. God forgive me,<br>Marry, and amen, how sound is she asleep!<br>I must needs wake her. Madam, madam, madam!<br>Ay, let the county take you in your bed;<br>He'll fright you up, i' faith. Will it not be?<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Undraws the curtains</em></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What, dress'd! and in your clothes! and down again!<br>I must needs wake you; Lady! lady! lady!<br>Alas, alas! Help, help! my lady's dead!<br>O, well-a-day, that ever I was born!<br>Some aqua vitae, ho! My lord! my lady!<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter LADY CAPULET</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What noise is here?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O lamentable day!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">What is the matter?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Look, look! O heavy day!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O me, O me! My child, my only life,<br>Revive, look up, or I will die with thee!<br>Help, help! Call help.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter CAPULET</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">For shame, bring Juliet forth; her lord is come.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">She's dead, deceased, she's dead; alack the day!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Alack the day, she's dead, she's dead, she's dead!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ha! let me see her: out, alas! she's cold:<br>Her blood is settled, and her joints are stiff;<br>Life and these lips have long been separated:<br>Death lies on her like an untimely frost<br>Upon the sweetest flower of all the field.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O lamentable day!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O woful time!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Death, that hath ta'en her hence to make me wail,<br>Ties up my tongue, and will not let me speak.<br></p><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><em>Enter FRIAR LAURENCE and PARIS, with Musicians</em></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Come, is the bride ready to go to church?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Ready to go, but never to return.<br>O son! the night before thy wedding-day<br>Hath Death lain with thy wife. There she lies,<br>Flower as she was, deflowered by him.<br>Death is my son-in-law, Death is my heir;<br>My daughter he hath wedded: I will die,<br>And leave him all; life, living, all is Death's.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Have I thought long to see this morning's face,<br>And doth it give me such a sight as this?<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>LADY CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Accursed, unhappy, wretched, hateful day!<br>Most miserable hour that e'er time saw<br>In lasting labour of his pilgrimage!<br>But one, poor one, one poor and loving child,<br>But one thing to rejoice and solace in,<br>And cruel death hath catch'd it from my sight!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>Nurse</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">O woe! O woful, woful, woful day!<br>Most lamentable day, most woful day,<br>That ever, ever, I did yet behold!<br>O day! O day! O day! O hateful day!<br>Never was seen so black a day as this:<br>O woful day, O woful day!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>PARIS</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Beguiled, divorced, wronged, spited, slain!<br>Most detestable death, by thee beguil'd,<br>By cruel cruel thee quite overthrown!<br>O love! O life! not life, but love in death!<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Despised, distressed, hated, martyr'd, kill'd!<br>Uncomfortable time, why camest thou now<br>To murder, murder our solemnity?<br>O child! O child! my soul, and not my child!<br>Dead art thou! Alack! my child is dead;<br>And with my child my joys are buried.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Peace, ho, for shame! confusion's cure lives not<br>In these confusions. Heaven and yourself<br>Had part in this fair maid; now heaven hath all,<br>And all the better is it for the maid:<br>Your part in her you could not keep from death,<br>But heaven keeps his part in eternal life.<br>The most you sought was her promotion;<br>For 'twas your heaven she should be advanced:<br>And weep ye now, seeing she is advanced<br>Above the clouds, as high as heaven itself?<br>O, in this love, you love your child so ill,<br>That you run mad, seeing that she is well:<br>She's not well married that lives married long;<br>But she's best married that dies married young.<br>Dry up your tears, and stick your rosemary<br>On this fair corse; and, as the custom is,<br>In all her best array bear her to church:<br>For though fond nature bids us an lament,<br>Yet nature's tears are reason's merriment.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>CAPULET</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">All things that we ordained festival,<br>Turn from their office to black funeral;<br>Our instruments to melancholy bells,<br>Our wedding cheer to a sad burial feast,<br>Our solemn hymns to sullen dirges change,<br>Our bridal flowers serve for a buried corse,<br>And all things change them to the contrary.<br></p></blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;"><strong>FRIAR LAURENCE</strong></p><blockquote><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">Sir, go you in;
